# Adobe Firefly Essential Training (2024)

> Generative AI is taking the world by storm, and Adobe has offered their own answer to the artificial intelligence revolution—Adobe Firefly. This family of generative AI models equips you with the potential to revolutionize your design skills and elevate your creative projects to unprecedented heights. In this course, join lifelong designer Bart Van de Wiele as he teaches you how to use Adobe Firef

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024) | 3h 48m | 27K learners

- [[Bart Van de Wiele]]

### 1. Firefly for Creatives

#### How does Firefly differ from other generative art solutions?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's take a moment to talk about what makes Adobe Firefly unique.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=4)** Now, first of all, Firefly is integrated within your existing Creative Cloud applications, so you can use your familiar user interface, like Photoshop and Illustrator, to use specific Firefly functionalities without having to leave the application, which can be a massive production booster.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=21)** The second reason why it's unique is because of how Firefly was created.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=25)** Adobe put out a very bold statement, saying that Firefly is designed to be commercially safe.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=31)** So this means that if you're looking to use Firefly to generate an image, then you can just go ahead and do so and use that image commercially.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=39)** And the reason why is because of the database, the algorithm that's fueling the Adobe Firefly experience because it's based on three things.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=48)** The first one is the Adobe Stock database.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=51)** So this is Adobe's own stock service that feeds about 400 million images to Adobe Firefly to help train and maintain the algorithm.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=61)** And these images have already been curated when they were initially submitted to the Adobe Stock Service.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=67)** Secondly, images available within the public space on the internet are also used for training.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=73)** So these are images where there's no copyright in the first place.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=77)** And then thirdly, images of which the copyright has expired, and this gives you a very, very decent database to work with to create images that are free from royalties and free from copyright.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=90)** Now, there's also a whole conversation about the relationship between using generative AI technology, and then harm and bias towards ethnic groups and other genders, so let me give you an example.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=102)** If you're looking to create an image of a nurse tending to a patient, will that nurse always be a woman?
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=109)** Or how about you wanting to create an image that involves religion?
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=113)** Which religion will be picked by Firefly?
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=116)** And there's just a whole variety of conversations that you can have around this, but Adobe has trained Firefly in such a way that there is, well, there should be more than enough diversity if you're looking at the results of specific images.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=129)** So let's take a look at just a couple of examples here of how Firefly is helping you keep these images commercially safe.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=137)** Now, the first one, I typed in the prompt, "Superman flying through the sky with a city in the background."

>

>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=177)** Let's look at a second example, Here, I typed in, "A Van Gogh style painting featuring beautiful, green fields, cows, and the blue sky."
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=186)** So the prompt concept remains, if you look at the results here, but there are no real references to real artists or the visual style inside of Adobe Firefly.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=196)** Now, you do have ways of bringing your own visual style references if you want, and you'll learn all about that later in this course, but just know that we're not specifically looking at images that are exact copies of a Van Gogh style, or any other famous painter for that matter.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=212)** And then lastly, I tried this one, "Disney's Mickey Mouse performing a magic spell."
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=218)** This also got flagged and I wasn't even able to create or use any of the Disney character names because this is intellectual property, so Firefly is shielding me from using those specific characters.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=230)** Instead, I had to reside to using a simple mouse performing a magic spell, so I have to change how I prompt things, and it's important that you realize how Firefly is basically trained and maintained just to match expectations about what is that you want to do and what is that you want to create.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/how-does-firefly-differ-from-other-generative-art-solutions?u=76281980&t=248)** So if you want to create celebrities in various poses or in fancy, fast cars and other types of scenes, then Firefly is probably not the solution for you, because it's really difficult to depict real people and real intellectual property products and characters.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (4), this, (2), interface (1), public (1)
> **Definitions:** means that (1), is a  (1)
> **Cross-References:** later in (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Is Firefly free?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Is Adobe Firefly free?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=2)** Well, the short answer is yes, but there are some things you do need to know.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=7)** Adobe Firefly uses its own currency system called generative credits, or, simply, generations.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=14)** And using any of Firefly's features will consume one of these credits.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=20)** For example, when you're using the text image features on the Firefly webpage, or when you're using the Generative Fill option in Photoshop, or how about text effects in Adobe Express, or how about when you're recoloring or creating vector artwork using Adobe Illustrator?
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=38)** Now, this all sounds fine, but how many credits do you have available?
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=42)** Because every single time you use any of these prompts, this will consume one credit.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=48)** Well, that depends on whether you are a paying subscriber or not.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=54)** If you use a free Firefly account, which you can register directly on the Firefly webpage, you will have a total of 25 credits available to you per month, where unused credits will not transfer into the next month.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=69)** But if you have some type of an Adobe subscription, for example, an Adobe Creative Cloud membership or even a single app membership, let's just say Photoshop, then you have many more credits available to you.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=82)** If you're not an active Creative Cloud subscriber, you can also directly subscribe to the Adobe Firefly service online or to other web services, like Adobe Express or even Adobe Stock.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=96)** When you are a paid subscriber, you will have access to several hundreds, or maybe even thousands of credits per user per month.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=106)** Now, the overall recommendation is to consult with Adobe's help pages, which clearly describes how many credits paid members are entitled to.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/is-firefly-free?u=76281980&t=115)** And if you are part of a larger enterprise, you can always talk to your Adobe representative or reseller to know just how many credits you have available within your entire team.

> **Definitions:** is a  (4), means that (2)
> **CLI Commands:** make (3)
> **Cross-References:** go back to (1), in the next (1)

>

> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/finding-similar-images-and-saving-favourites?u=76281980&t=356)** And you can keep fine tuning your results as you see fit, and you can even start to add more effects to your result to get to a different type of image.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/finding-similar-images-and-saving-favourites?u=76281980&t=364)** Now, here I can see that I have a different result where I am, again, replicating the same perspective with these different pillars, the stairs, a humanoid, and the fish going through the city.

> **[6:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/finding-similar-images-and-saving-favourites?u=76281980&t=375)** So next time you're trying to create something similar looking based on a prompt, remember to click this option here in the edit menu and then choose generate similar.

#### Using a Style reference
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-style-reference?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-style-reference?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There is one final setting that we have not discussed yet, which is the match style setting.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-style-reference?u=76281980&t=6)** Now, match style allows you to assign a secondary image to your prompt, just like a structure reference.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-style-reference?u=76281980&t=12)** However, this time Firefly will mimic the visual style of the image and apply that style to your prompt.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-style-reference?u=76281980&t=20)** So this means that the shapes, the style, texture, color, theme, anything that makes your image look unique will be copied and applied to the prompt that you're currently creating.

### 4. Image Magic with Generative Fill

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's look at what I think is one of the most interesting features in Adobe Firefly, Generative Fill.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=6)** Now, in the previous few chapters, you learned how to use a text prompt to create an entire image from scratch.

> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=13)** However, what do you do when you want to selectively edit just a part of an existing image using generative AI?

> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=25)** This technology allows you to surgically alter just a part of an image by making simple text selections and then prompting what you want to generate in those areas.

#### Introducing Generative Expand
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-expand?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Allow me to introduce the final option or final feature here within the generative fill technology stack using Adobe Firefly.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=8)** I'm starting out here with a familiar scene.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/introducing-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=10)** This is the breakfast scene that we worked on before, but I did go in and made a few additional changes.
>

> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=227)** And again, you just go ahead and pick a different version anytime you like.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=231)** Now I'm going to go ahead and save this document by choosing File, Save.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=235)** I want to just quickly point out one little detail.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=238)** Now, when you start to generate additional versions of this specific generative layer, you will be adding a lot of data to your Photoshop file.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=247)** Now, in this instance, I have six different versions of an elephant, but I'm really only interested in using just this one.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=256)** However, if I take a look here at this document, you can see that this document, elephant-start, is 37 megabytes.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=263)** If I were to go back here and then just delete any of these other variations by simply clicking the trash can icon, let's get rid of this one, let's delete this one, delete this one, and those ones, and you simply re-save the file, and you go back to the finder, you will see that now I only have 29 megabytes.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=283)** Now, this is a very small generation, I got to say, this is only a very small canvas, it's a very light document.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=290)** However, if you are creating large generations and large images with many different versions, you can easily add a few dozen or even a few hundred megabytes to your file, and it's just data sitting there, you're not even using that.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=306)** So when you've made up your mind, just go ahead and delete the versions you don't really want.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=311)** But be careful because you cannot undo that specific command, which means once deleted, it is gone forever, so be careful what you do.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-fill?u=76281980&t=320)** But for now, we just get to sit back and enjoy this really cool image of an elephant walking through the streets of Paris.

>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/generating-images?u=76281980&t=353)** Anything that is larger than that is going to look upscaled and might appear a little bit pixelated.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/generating-images?u=76281980&t=359)** Now, if I look at the file dimensions from this specific document by going into Image and then Image Size, I can see that I am within those boundaries of 2048 pixels, which means that the resolution I'm seeing here is exactly what Firefly can give me.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/generating-images?u=76281980&t=376)** But if I started out with a document that measures, for example, 4,000 by 6,000 pixels, then the end result might not look that great because Firefly will generate an image that measures a maximum of 2048, and it will then upscale that to match the current canvas size.
>
> **[6:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/generating-images?u=76281980&t=395)** So keep that in mind when you're generating images that the resolution might sometimes look a little bit off simply because the canvas size that you've set in Photoshop is bigger than the maximum resolution that Firefly version three, at least at the time of this recording, can actually achieve by using text-to-image directly in Photoshop.

#### Using Generative Expand
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let me show you how you can use generative expand directly within Adobe Photoshop.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=5)** To get started, simply open up koala-start.psd and then switch to the crop tool to initiate this process.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=14)** Now, before you do anything, it's important to realize that Photoshop has three different methods of cropping images.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=21)** So if you go to the top of the screen, be sure to change the fill option from transparent to generative expand.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-generative-expand?u=76281980&t=29)** Now I'm going to take a step back by zooming out by pressing command minus or CTRL minus on Windows, and then simply choose the ratio that you want to use.
>

#### Using a reference image

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you've gone through all the previous chapters in this course, then I'm absolutely convinced that you came across this image.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=7)** We named this person Edward, and Edward just came back from safari.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, unfortunately for him, summer's over, vacation is over, and it's time to head into winter, which means it's time for Edward to put on a warm winter coat, and I know exactly which one.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=23)** a warm winter coat, and I know exactly which one.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=24)** If you look at the project folder, there's this image called reference.jpg, and this is what the image looks like.

>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=43)** And this is where we can start to use reference images directly within Adobe Photoshop Beta.

> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=54)** Now, everything starts with a selection, and it's really important that, for this selection, that you make a selection based on the outline of the coat that this person should be wearing.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=68)** In other words, don't base your selection on the current outfit, base your selection on the outfit that you want this person to wear.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=76)** For example, if I want to put in a coat in this image and this coat has a hoodie, then I have to make sure that I include space for that hoodie as part of my selection.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-a-reference-image?u=76281980&t=89)** Let me show you how that works.
>

>

### 6. Using Firefly in Adobe Express

#### Using text effects in Adobe Express
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-text-effects-in-adobe-express?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-text-effects-in-adobe-express?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's create a new project that uses text effects here inside of Adobe Express.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-text-effects-in-adobe-express?u=76281980&t=5)** Now to get started, simply navigate to express.[adobe.com](https://adobe.com) and then click the plus icon here to start a brand new project.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/using-text-effects-in-adobe-express?u=76281980&t=14)** I'll choose Landscape as a standard size because this is just about applying text effects.
>

### 7. Using Firefly in Adobe Illustrator

>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/controlling-styles?u=76281980&t=294)** And so, once this has been set using a picker, it doesn't quite matter where this rectangle is now positioned, The only thing you have to do now is just type in the prompt and then hit the Generate option again to use that style for anything that you now generate, regardless of where this shape is now being positioned on the art board and whatever artwork might be in its vicinity.
>

#### Solution: Text to vectors
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/solution-text-to-vectors?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/solution-text-to-vectors?u=76281980&t=0)** (lively music)

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/solution-text-to-vectors?u=76281980&t=9)** So the idea was to work around a science fiction alien and space theme overall, and you also need to use at least two different types of text to vector settings.

> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/solution-text-to-vectors?u=76281980&t=20)** Now, let me show you what I did.
>

### 8. Ethical Generative AI

#### AI-generated images and ethics
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] How do you combine the ease of use of Generative AI with the battle on misinformation?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=6)** And this is an important subject for society, and it's also one that Adobe is very actively participating in.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=13)** So, now that you've learned how powerful Firefly is, you might ask yourself how this technology can affect trust on the internet, or you might better understand the need to verify information sources in the media, or what is Adobe doing to make sure that Adobe Firefly will help uphold ethical standards?
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=34)** Now, these questions and concerns are being addressed by an organization called the Content Authenticity Initiative.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=42)** And this organization was first announced by Adobe back in 2019.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=48)** And since their first announcement, hundreds of members have joined the cause, including Microsoft, BBC, Intel, and many more.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=57)** Now, this coalition is on a mission to help address misinformation and content authenticity at scale.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=65)** But how are they doing this?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=67)** Well, they're doing this by introducing the world's first tamper-evident metadata for images called Content Credentials.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=75)** Now, you can look at Content Credentials as a type of digital nutrition label for digital images.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=81)** So, adding this metadata to images will help build credibility and trust by sharing the details about the creative process that is required to create the image in the first place.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=94)** And by providing this metadata, you can describe the history and the image provenance, and this system can help the spread of misinformation over time.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=104)** So, whenever you download an image from the Adobe Firefly website, these Content Credentials will always be applied to the download file automatically.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=115)** And this happens even when you're using Firefly directly in applications like Photoshop.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=121)** And you can even activate the same Content Credentials in Photoshop projects that don't even use Adobe Firefly technology to help create these digital breadcrumbs that proven image's history.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=135)** Now, once you've attached these Content Credentials, the receiver of your file can then verify your Content Credentials online via the Content Authenticity's website.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=146)** And this means that you have the ability to see the editing history of a received image and also grant others a higher level of transparency when you are supplying images to someone yourself.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/ai-generated-images-and-ethics?u=76281980&t=160)** Now, if you're interested in learning more, I recommend you take a look at the Content Authenticity's Initiative, and look at their webpage for more information.

> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/downloading-images-and-viewing-content-credentials?u=76281980&t=339)** It's actually giving me a pop-up already that says publish the credentials.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/downloading-images-and-viewing-content-credentials?u=76281980&t=342)** It says you can publish your files content credentials to the content credentials cloud when exporting instead of attaching them to your files.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/downloading-images-and-viewing-content-credentials?u=76281980&t=350)** Now, this makes the edit and activity history more persistent and recoverable and keeps the file size smaller.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/downloading-images-and-viewing-content-credentials?u=76281980&t=357)** So it's basically saying, if you want, I can take all that history and publish that to a cloud instead of just attaching that locally to the file, which might make the file size grow, or which might enable you to, sometimes, disable or deactivate the content credentials functionality, which might result in missed steps being recorded.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/downloading-images-and-viewing-content-credentials?u=76281980&t=378)** So this is basically what you can do.

> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=152)** So if I were to drag and drop this purse into Firefly, either as a JPEG or as a transparent PNG, it allows me to position this somewhere on this virtual canvas.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=162)** And then the next phase, it allows me to type in the prompt I'm looking for, for example, in this case, a marble table in a living room.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=170)** And it's going to take that product and put it into the scene based on where I specified the product should appear.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=178)** So on the left hand side, it's actually using a type of extension based on the structure reference that we've learned here in this course, and it's just going to combine that product now directly here within this image.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=190)** Now, what makes this unique is the following.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=193)** If you look at some of the details of this actual render, you can see that it now generated a shadow that sits just underneath the purse, which wasn't there in the original image.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=203)** We had an image without any shadows.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=207)** And also notice the reflection on the marble, and that is what makes object compositions unique because you simply drag and drop in your product, you type in the circumstances, maybe your product should be sitting on whatever as part of an ice sculpture, again, you'll have reflections and you'll have shadows, the lighting will match, et cetera.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=228)** So this is just one application of what is you can do if you extend these functionalities in Firefly.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=234)** Now, just so you know that there are a couple of use cases that are really, really interesting if you look at this extra technology, not just the object compositions, but everything else, the automation, using your own systems, using your own data as part of a custom model.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=248)** So for example, you can even choose to automate banner creation.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=252)** What if you have a banner in Photoshop that measures very specific pixel dimensions and you have to create a square version and maybe a vertical or a horizontal version, different sizes?
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=264)** What you can do is you can now use generative expand in combination with APIs and other automation techniques just to bulk generate all these different versions in one go.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=275)** Product visualization is something that you can do by using your own custom model or by using the object composition that we've just discussed.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=283)** And you can even do batch post-processing where you basically go in and you have the ability to use a combination of Firefly prompts, you can remove backgrounds from images, replace 'em with a Firefly prompt, expand the canvas, even automate this by applying Lightroom presets.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=300)** The sky is kind of the limit here.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=302)** So all of these are like little custom projects and this technology exists today.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/adobe-firefly-essential-training-2024/where-to-go-from-here?u=76281980&t=306)** So if you do have any questions about all these different things here, I would suggest you take a look at the Adobe help pages to get started.
